[1mNAME[0m[m
       find - search for files in a directory hierarchy[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mfind[0m  [-H] [-L] [-P] [-D debugopts] [-Olevel] [starting-[m
       point...] [expression][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       This manual page documents the GNU version of [1mfind[0m.  GNU[m
       [1mfind[0m  searches  the  directory tree rooted at each given[m
       starting-point by evaluating the given  expression  from[m
       left to right, according to the rules of precedence (see[m
       section OPERATORS), until the outcome is known (the left[m
       hand  side is false for [4mand[24m operations, true for [4mor[24m), at[m
       which point [1mfind[0m moves on to the next file name.  If  no[m
       starting-point is specified, `.' is assumed.[m
[m
       If  you  are using [1mfind[0m in an environment where security[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 11 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       is important (for example if you are using it to  search[m
       directories  that  are  writable  by  other  users), you[m
       should read the `Security Considerations' chapter of the[m
       findutils  documentation,  which is called [1mFinding[0m [1mFiles[0m[m
       and comes with findutils.  That document also includes a[m
       lot more detail and discussion than this manual page, so[m
       you may find it a more useful source of information.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       The [1m-H[0m, [1m-L[0m and [1m-P[0m options control the treatment of  symâ€[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 21 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       bolic links.  Command-line arguments following these are[m
       taken to be names of files or directories  to  be  examâ€[m
       ined,  up to the first argument that begins with `-', or[m
       the argument `(' or `!'.  That argument and any  followâ€[m
       ing  arguments are taken to be the expression describing[m
       what is to be searched for.  If no paths are given,  the[m
       current  directory  is used.  If no expression is given,[m
       the expression [1m-print[0m is used (but you  should  probably[m
       consider using [1m-print0[0m instead, anyway).[m
[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 31 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       This  manual  page  talks about `options' within the exâ€[m
       pression list.  These options control the  behaviour  of[m
       [1mfind[0m  but  are specified immediately after the last path[m
       name.  The five `real' options [1m-H[0m, [1m-L[0m,  [1m-P[0m,  [1m-D[0m  and  [1m-O[0m[m
       must  appear  before  the first path name, if at all.  A[m
       double dash [1m--[0m could theoretically  be  used  to  signal[m
       that  any  remaining arguments are not options, but this[m
       does not really work due to the way [1mfind[0m determines  the[m
       end  of  the  following  path arguments: it does that by[m
       reading until an expression argument comes  (which  also[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 41 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       starts with a `-').  Now, if a path argument would start[m
       with a `-', then [1mfind[0m would treat it as expression arguâ€[m
       ment instead.  Thus, to ensure that all start points are[m
       taken as such, and especially to prevent  that  wildcard[m
       patterns  expanded  by the calling shell are not mistakâ€[m
       enly treated as expression arguments,  it  is  generally[m
       safer to prefix wildcards or dubious path names with eiâ€[m
       ther `./' or to use absolute path  names  starting  with[m
       '/'.   Alternatively,  it  is generally safe though non-[m
       portable to use the GNU option [1m-files0-from[0m to pass  arâ€[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 51 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       bitrary starting points to [1mfind[0m.[m
[m
       -P     Never follow symbolic links.  This is the default[m
              behaviour.  When [1mfind[0m examines or prints informaâ€[m
              tion  about  files,  and  the  file is a symbolic[m
              link, the information used shall  be  taken  from[m
              the properties of the symbolic link itself.[m
[m
       -L     Follow  symbolic  links.   When  [1mfind[0m examines or[m
              prints information about files,  the  information[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 61 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              used  shall  be  taken from the properties of the[m
              file to which the link points, not from the  link[m
              itself  (unless  it  is a broken symbolic link or[m
              [1mfind[0m is unable to examine the file to  which  the[m
              link   points).    Use  of  this  option  implies[m
              [1m-noleaf[0m.  If you later use the [1m-P[0m option, [1m-noleaf[0m[m
              will  still be in effect.  If [1m-L[0m is in effect and[m
              [1mfind[0m discovers a symbolic link to a  subdirectory[m
              during its search, the subdirectory pointed to by[m
              the symbolic link will be searched.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 71 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m
              When the [1m-L[0m option is in effect, the [1m-type[0m prediâ€[m
              cate  will  always  match against the type of the[m
              file that a symbolic link points to  rather  than[m
              the link itself (unless the symbolic link is broâ€[m
              ken).  Actions that can cause symbolic  links  to[m
              become  broken while [1mfind[0m is executing (for examâ€[m
              ple [1m-delete[0m) can give rise  to  confusing  behavâ€[m
              iour.   Using  [1m-L[0m  causes  the [1m-lname[0m and [1m-ilname[0m[m
              predicates always to return false.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 81 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m
       -H     Do not follow symbolic links, except  while  proâ€[m
              cessing  the  command  line arguments.  When [1mfind[0m[m
              examines or prints information about  files,  the[m
              information  used shall be taken from the properâ€[m
              ties of the symbolic link itself.  The  only  exâ€[m
              ception  to  this behaviour is when a file speciâ€[m
              fied on the command line is a symbolic link,  and[m
              the  link  can  be resolved.  For that situation,[m
              the information used is taken from  whatever  the[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 91 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              link  points  to (that is, the link is followed).[m
              The information about the link itself is used  as[m
              a fallback if the file pointed to by the symbolic[m
              link cannot be examined.  If [1m-H[0m is in effect  and[m
              one of the paths specified on the command line is[m
              a symbolic link to a directory, the  contents  of[m
              that directory will be examined (though of course[m
              [1m-maxdepth[0m [1m0[0m would prevent this).[m
[m
       If more than one of [1m-H[0m, [1m-L[0m and  [1m-P[0m  is  specified,  each[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 101 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       overrides the others; the last one appearing on the comâ€[m
       mand line takes effect.  Since it is the default, the [1m-P[0m[m
       option  should  be considered to be in effect unless eiâ€[m
       ther [1m-H[0m or [1m-L[0m is specified.[m
[m
       GNU [1mfind[0m frequently stats files during the processing of[m
       the command line itself, before any searching has begun.[m
       These options also affect how those arguments  are  proâ€[m
       cessed.   Specifically, there are a number of tests that[m
       compare files listed on the command line against a  file[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 111 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       we  are  currently  considering.  In each case, the file[m
       specified on the command line will  have  been  examined[m
       and some of its properties will have been saved.  If the[m
       named file is in fact a symbolic link, and the [1m-P[0m option[m
       is  in  effect (or if neither [1m-H[0m nor [1m-L[0m were specified),[m
       the information used for the comparison  will  be  taken[m
       from the properties of the symbolic link.  Otherwise, it[m
       will be taken from the properties of the file  the  link[m
       points  to.  If [1mfind[0m cannot follow the link (for example[m
       because it  has  insufficient  privileges  or  the  link[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 121 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       points to a nonexistent file) the properties of the link[m
       itself will be used.[m
[m
       When the [1m-H[0m or [1m-L[0m options are in  effect,  any  symbolic[m
       links  listed as the argument of [1m-newer[0m will be dereferâ€[m
       enced, and the timestamp will be taken from the file  to[m
       which  the symbolic link points.  The same consideration[m
       applies to [1m-newerXY[0m, [1m-anewer[0m and [1m-cnewer[0m.[m
[m
       The [1m-follow[0m option has a similar effect to [1m-L[0m, though it[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 131 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       takes  effect at the point where it appears (that is, if[m
       [1m-L[0m is not used but [1m-follow[0m is, any  symbolic  links  apâ€[m
       pearing after [1m-follow[0m on the command line will be derefâ€[m
       erenced, and those before it will not).[m
[m
       -D debugopts[m
              Print diagnostic information; this can be helpful[m
              to  diagnose  problems with why [1mfind[0m is not doing[m
              what you want.  The list of debug options  should[m
              be  comma  separated.  Compatibility of the debug[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 141 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              options is not  guaranteed  between  releases  of[m
              findutils.   For  a  complete list of valid debug[m
              options, see the output of [1mfind[0m  [1m-D[0m [1mhelp[0m.   Valid[m
              debug options include[m
[m
              exec   Show  diagnostic  information  relating to[m
                     -exec, -execdir, -ok and -okdir[m
[m
              opt    Prints diagnostic information relating  to[m
                     the  optimisation  of the expression tree;[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 151 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K                     see the -O option.[m
[m
              rates  Prints a summary indicating how often each[m
                     predicate succeeded or failed.[m
[m
              search Navigate the directory tree verbosely.[m
[m
              stat   Print  messages as files are examined with[m
                     the [1mstat[0m and [1mlstat[0m system calls.  The [1mfind[0m[m
                     program tries to minimise such calls.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 161 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m
              tree   Show  the  expression tree in its original[m
                     and optimised form.[m
[m
              all    Enable all of the other debug options (but[m
                     [1mhelp[0m).[m
[m
              help   Explain the debugging options.[m
[m
       -Olevel[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 171 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              Enables query optimisation.  The [1mfind[0m program reâ€[m
              orders tests to speed up execution while preservâ€[m
              ing  the overall effect; that is, predicates with[m
              side effects are not reordered relative  to  each[m
              other.  The optimisations performed at each optiâ€[m
              misation level are as follows.[m
[m
              0      Equivalent to optimisation level 1.[m
[m
              1      This is the default optimisation level and[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 181 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K                     corresponds  to the traditional behaviour.[m
                     Expressions are reordered  so  that  tests[m
                     based  only on the names of files (for exâ€[m
                     ample  [1m-name[0m  and  [1m-regex[0m)  are  performed[m
                     first.[m
[m
              2      Any  [1m-type[0m  or  [1m-xtype[0m tests are performed[m
                     after any tests based only on the names of[m
                     files,  but  before any tests that require[m
                     information from the inode.  On many  modâ€[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 191 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K                     ern  versions  of Unix, file types are reâ€[m
                     turned by [1mreaddir()[0m and  so  these  prediâ€[m
                     cates  are  faster to evaluate than prediâ€[m
                     cates which need to stat the  file  first.[m
                     If  you  use the [1m-fstype[0m [4mFOO[24m predicate and[m
                     specify a filesystem type [4mFOO[24m which is not[m
                     known (that is, present in `/etc/mtab') at[m
                     the time [1mfind[0m starts,  that  predicate  is[m
                     equivalent to [1m-false[0m.[m
[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 201 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              3      At this optimisation level, the full cost-[m
                     based query optimiser is enabled.  The orâ€[m
                     der  of  tests  is  modified so that cheap[m
                     (i.e. fast) tests are performed first  and[m
                     more  expensive  ones are performed later,[m
                     if  necessary.   Within  each  cost  band,[m
                     predicates  are evaluated earlier or later[m
                     according to whether they  are  likely  to[m
                     succeed  or not.  For [1m-o[0m, predicates which[m
                     are likely to succeed are  evaluated  earâ€[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 211 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K                     lier,  and  for  [1m-a[0m,  predicates which are[m
                     likely to fail are evaluated earlier.[m
[m
              The cost-based optimiser has a fixed idea of  how[m
              likely  any  given  test  is to succeed.  In some[m
              cases the probability takes account of  the  speâ€[m
              cific nature of the test (for example, [1m-type[0m [1mf[0m is[m
              assumed  to  be  more  likely  to  succeed   than[m
              [1m-type[0m [1mc[0m).   The cost-based optimiser is currently[m
              being evaluated.  If it does not actually improve[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 221 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              the  performance  of  [1mfind[0m,  it  will  be removed[m
              again.  Conversely, optimisations that  prove  to[m
              be  reliable, robust and effective may be enabled[m
              at lower optimisation levels over time.  However,[m
              the default behaviour (i.e. optimisation level 1)[m
              will not be changed in the 4.3.x release  series.[m
              The  findutils  test  suite runs all the tests on[m
              [1mfind[0m at each optimisation level and ensures  that[m
              the result is the same.[m
[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 231 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[1mEXPRESSION[0m[m
       The  part of the command line after the list of starting[m
       points is the [4mexpression[24m.  This is a kind of query specâ€[m
       ification  describing  how we match files and what we do[m
       with the files that were matched.  An expression is comâ€[m
       posed of a sequence of things:[m
[m
       Tests  Tests  return  a  true or false value, usually on[m
              the basis of some property of a file we are  conâ€[m
              sidering.   The  [1m-empty[0m  test for example is true[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 241 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              only when the current file is empty.[m
[m
       Actions[m
              Actions have side effects (such as printing someâ€[m
              thing  on  the standard output) and return either[m
              true or false, usually based on  whether  or  not[m
              they are successful.  The [1m-print[0m action for examâ€[m
              ple prints the name of the current  file  on  the[m
              standard output.[m
[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 251 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       Global options[m
              Global  options affect the operation of tests and[m
              actions specified on  any  part  of  the  command[m
              line.   Global  options  always return true.  The[m
              [1m-depth[0m option for example makes [1mfind[0m traverse the[m
              file system in a depth-first order.[m
[m
       Positional options[m
              Positional  options  affect only tests or actions[m
              which follow them.  Positional options always reâ€[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 261 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              turn  true.  The [1m-regextype[0m option for example is[m
              positional, specifying the regular expression diâ€[m
              alect  for regular expressions occurring later on[m
              the command line.[m
[m
       Operators[m
              Operators join together the  other  items  within[m
              the  expression.   They  include  for  example [1m-o[0m[m
              (meaning logical  OR)  and  [1m-a[0m  (meaning  logical[m
              AND).   Where  an  operator is missing, [1m-a[0m is asâ€[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 271 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              sumed.[m
[m
       The [1m-print[0m action is performed on all  files  for  which[m
       the  whole expression is true, unless it contains an acâ€[m
       tion other than [1m-prune[0m or [1m-quit[0m.  Actions which  inhibit[m
       the  default  [1m-print[0m  are [1m-delete[0m, [1m-exec[0m, [1m-execdir[0m, [1m-ok[0m,[m
       [1m-okdir[0m,  [1m-fls[0m,  [1m-fprint[0m,  [1m-fprintf[0m,  [1m-ls[0m,   [1m-print[0m   and[m
       [1m-printf[0m.[m
[m
       The  [1m-delete[0m  action  also acts like an option (since it[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 281 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       implies [1m-depth[0m).[m
[m
   [1mPOSITIONAL[0m [1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       Positional options always return true.  They affect only[m
       tests occurring later on the command line.[m
[m
       -daystart[m
              Measure  times (for [1m-amin[0m, [1m-atime[0m, [1m-cmin[0m, [1m-ctime[0m,[m
              [1m-mmin[0m, and [1m-mtime[0m) from the  beginning  of  today[m
              rather  than from 24 hours ago.  This option only[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 291 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              affects tests which appear later on  the  command[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 292 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              line.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 293 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 294 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       -follow[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 295 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              Deprecated;  use the [1m-L[0m option instead.  Dereferâ€[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 296 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              ence symbolic links.  Implies [1m-noleaf[0m.  The [1m-folâ€[0m[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 297 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              [1mlow[0m  option affects only those tests which appear[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 298 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              after it on the command line.  Unless the  [1m-H[0m  or[m

[7m.bash_history[27m[K[K[?1l>[?1049l[23;0;0t[?2004h[94m~ (B[m$ [H[2J[94m~ (B[m$ help history
[?2004lhistory: history [-c] [-d offset] [n] or history -anrw [filename] or history -ps arg [arg...]
    Display or manipulate the history list.
    
    Display the history list with line numbers, prefixing each modified
    entry with a `*'.  An argument of N lists only the last N entries.
    
    Options:
      -c	clear the history list by deleting all of the entries
      -d offset	delete the history entry at position OFFSET. Negative
    		offsets count back from the end of the history list
    
      -a	append history lines from this session to the history file
      -n	read all history lines not already read from the history file
    		and append them to the history list
      -r	read the history file and append the contents to the history
    		list
      -w	write the current history to the history file
    
      -p	perform history expansion on each ARG and display the result
    		without storing it in the history list
      -s	append the ARGs to the history list as a single entry
    
    If FILENAME is given, it is used as the history file.  Otherwise,
    if HISTFILE has a value, that is used, else ~/.bash_history.
    
    If the HISTTIMEFORMAT variable is set and not null, its value is used
    as a format string for strftime(3) to print the time stamp associated
    with each displayed history entry.  No time stamps are printed otherwise.
    
    Exit Status:
    Returns success unless an invalid option is given or an error occurs.

       ture  is  enabled by default for interactive shells, and[m

       active shells do not perform history  expansion  by  deâ€[m

       mands quickly.[m
